--- 帖子 #797 ---
So while not much is happening with the Day charts, time for more back testing and training charts.

The EJ Day chart shows a great Set Up Candle SUC with the Entry Candle EC two candle later.

Usual criteria for TP1 and SL or as a more cautious approach an option can be to use 1XATR7 for TP1 with the SL set to the previous swing H.

Now for the fun.  Once you have entered on the Day Chart, switch to the H4 to manage Add-Ons as they occur more frequently than on the Day Charts.

Add-On Candles AOC occur on the fractal lows.  Not all of them will trigger - in the H4 chart, AOC 2 and AOC 4 do not trigger.

For this scenario, TP1 would have triggered and achieved 2XATR7 = 280pips, or for the more cautious approach 140pips

TP2 would currently be achieving 300 pips and would still be open as would the Add-Ons

AOC 1 = 170pips

AOC 3 = 120pips

AOC 5 = BE

The benefits of this approach are that you can scale into a successful trend by managing entries on the H4.

For an ongoing pip management strategy the SL would need to be moved (depending on your risk tolerance and if you survived the DrawDown DD of 140pips during 4/9) seeing as there have been no new Fractal Highs on the H4.  My approach would be to take a recent swing H - The 12:00 candle from 4/10 would be reasonable and this would allow approx 90 pips of breathing space and would only risk 50 pips on each open position based on the current price.

When checking on the Day Chart, the last major support level (Fractal Low) is currently acting as a stall point at 105.62.  If this is cleared with a candle closing, that will keep the PA below the Day 100ema and the 200ema.

Possible next support level would then be another 200pips away with more pips possible.

Back test this as an additional strategy and get comfortable with identifying Add-Ons.

As promised, here is a losing trade and my process for analyzing why / lessons learned / root cause!

Initially the APB changed colour and indicated a bounce off of the 200ema.

So, what went wrong?

TDI looked promising with a cross of red/green and a cross of the Down Zone.

What in hindsight may have been warning signs?

1. RSI 10 was still low @ 41 - should really be closer to 50 or >50

2. The ATR1 for the colour change was well below the ATR7; ATR1 was 60% of ATR7 - probably too low a ratio on reflection - should be 80% or higher

3. SL set at Swing Low and not at 2XATR which would have kept me in the game and would now be showing a profit of 75 pips - all part of the black arts regarding money management and risk/reward settings

On reflection then:

A) RSI 10 needs to be near or above 50

B) ATR1 for the Set Up Candle (SUC) needs to be closer to the ATR7 value

C) SL needs to be set @ 2XATR7 and not Swing Low

D) TDI crosses can get you in the poop!

Or, as a well regarded 4X trader commented "The majority of retail traders get the direction correct, but not the timing!"

Pay the 4x gods and move on to the next one

--- 帖子 #814 ---
Reversals are always a tricky area to spot and gauge correctly - I will use the APB for a colour change on the day and then watch for PA to confirm the move on the following day - maybe even drop down to the H4 to confirm PA.  Sometimes this can take a couple of candles to confirm.

Additionally I will use candle reversal patterns from standard candles/bars as well as break outs from Inside Bar set-ups.

Significant breaks through 100ema and/or 200ema are always a good sign.

For me the charts give some good signals - Large Candle which sets up inside bars for several days, 100ema and 200ema running closely together with no angle and the TDI hovering around 50 - also the RSI10 hovering around 50.

--- 帖子 #820 ---
General rules are avoid shorting in the 32 area and going long in the 68 area.

This will also be true for when the RSI10 has been down around the 20-30 area or 70-80 area.  Hence the phrases Over-Sold and Over-Bought.  This just means that the pair is probably getting close to S/R levels and/or the 100ema and 200ema.

Sometimes it is best to watch.

I would say that I do not take new entries in those areas as this probably is several candles after a coulour change or an initial tdi cross.

If there is still a strong trend, these entries can be great for add-ons.

I am currently not trading due to time constraints - should be back in the saddle in a couple of weeks.

Keep the backtesting going - it will show you what patterns to avoid and which are your higher probability trades.

I want to show here a simple method for trending any pair on the 4H timeframe.

It uses simple indicators: Osma and Alligator lines for trending plus a Round Numbers indicator for entries

As trend is down (price below alligator lines and osma negative) we take shorts at every up retracement to the round numbers (see arrows in pics).

Viceversa for long.

It's simple, clean and works out good also in choppy markets, identifying clearly the ranges.

regards

Alex

--- 帖子 #843 ---
Still tracking GU lower and it is now nearing major support area.

Pip Protection Policy is something that I am running where I close out TP1 early as a trade loses momentum / enters areas on Major S/R.

This is often a strategy that I use for Friday trades that start to stall so that you can take some pips out of the market and leave the second position running with a break even SL.

Big E would talk about closing positions that started to pull back and then look for re-entry positions, so this is an adaptation of that approach.

My approach with running two entries per trade and the ATR7 approach is from dcginc.  Remember, if you run with two positions and close the first for profit and move the 2nd SL to BE, it is still a good pip day and it removes the stress for leaving 2 positions open over the weekend.

--- 帖子 #848 ---
As an example, I'll use the current GU day chart for this one.

Many folks use MA crosses and whether they are EMAs (exponential) or simple/smoothed (SMAs), there is little difference, especially on the larger ones.

The classic MA cross for entry signals is 3/8 - Lawgirl had a great thread running on that approach, and Big E was initially using the 5ema as a signal once PA closed above / below.

Big E had a couple of strategies before finally settling on the TMS with the TDI cross and one of those used 23/233 (I use 21/200)  Once the 21 clears the 200, the trend should be good for add-ons.

With the 100 and 200ema often acting as dynamic S/R levels you are looking for a bounce away from the ema, or a cross and close above / below (breakthrough).

With the GU chart examples, you see a change in direction on 4/16 which starts to pull away from the 100/200emas (TDI cross would have confirmed 4/18).  21ema is already above the 100/200 which would favour a long move.  This runs for 400 pips before hitting the brakes.

So now you are in a position of no longer moving away from the 100/200emas (so rules with longer term emas don't really work here!) - there was a TDI cross after 5/1 (and this would be from the overbought zone >68) and now the direction starts to reverse and fall back towards the 100/200ema.  Basically, look to the 100/200emas as gravity in this instance, pulling the price back to earth.

So now the decision is when to take the reverse on the day chart.  You can take the TDI cross, which would have got you in on 5/1, 5/2, or following the RSI rules of waiting until <50, then you have to wait for the pause around 5/7 to 5/14 and then take an entry.  With this reversal, it has such strength that it punches through the 100/200ema, pauses and then goes again, this time moving away from the 100/200ema.  Now the question will be at what point will the 100/200ema pull the price back again and set up the next reversal.

Mostly, this is down to trading style - trend traders will trade away from the 100/200ema and the reversal traders look for reversal signals to head back towards the 100/200ema.  This is where having a combination of approaches will pay off.

Once there is a 300 to 500 pip gap between price and 100/200ema, there will usually be a pause and eventual reversal - or, the price will consolidate for a while and allow the 100/200emas time to move to the price.

Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #870 ---
As you peruse the FF threads, you will come across many folks that have multiple trades running and as a result they post very impressive pips.

The primary thing to have clear in your mind as you read these threads, is how the money management strategies play out.

If you trade multiple pairs simultaneously, then your risk reward ratios get dramatically affected.  As you stack up multiple trades, so do you stack up the risk portion of the equation.

Run the numbers and make sure your account can withstand the losses and then understand how long it will take you to make the losses back. If you lose 25% on a trade, you need to gain 33% on the next trades to break even - a 50% loss means that you now need a 100% win to get back to where you were.  Do you have a money management plan?  Do you follow it?  What happens if you have multiples of losses?

Essentially, don't get greedy.  I would prefer to have one successful entry and miss four than load up multiples and then have them reverse on a bad piece of news, or adverse market reaction. "Pigs get fat, Hogs get slaughtered" - be a pig, not a hog!

Once you have a trade in profit and protected, then look for additional trades, or stick with the trade you have and look for Add-Ons.

--- 帖子 #894 ---
the strength indicator shows which currency is  strongest so if usd is at the top of the list and eur is at the bottom of the list, then eur/usd would be a good currency pair to trade short

For the RSI indicator this shows what the RSI is doing on the various time frames, so if the RSI is showing above 50 for all time frames, then going long would be a good idea.  If the RSI is below 50 on H4 / D but above 50 on M, then verify PA and S/R levels - should be good for a short trade.

I just use these as a heads up - all my decisions come from PA.

--- 帖子 #897 ---
I like the golf analogies for the discussion of systems versus expertise.

There are multiple swing techniques and you only have to read any of the multiple golf magazines to find that each coach is promoting a different slant on essentially one goal - accuracy and repeatability. There is no holy grail in golf, or any other particular skill except for learning, experience and application. discover what approach works in any particular scenario and perfect the approach.

All of the retail training companies are there for one purpose - selling training materials and to ultimately generate a passive income from subscription services, so essentially there is going to be an upsell - "join our exclusive platinum members only benefits club/group".

Some of the retail training companies may very well be successful in using their own systems, but I guarantee they make more money selling product than they do in trading. Residual/Passive income is the key (Trump / Kiyosaki).

Maybe cynical - probably not.

From all of the FF threads that start out with a "pure" approach / system, most get corrupted by a profusion of indicators which only serve to confuse and distort the approach.

All indicators are in fact lagging (historical) - they are based on moving averages based on a sample size of previous prices / L/H / closes or they are based on more complicated algorithms. There are no true leading (predictive) indicators. There are numerous examples of robots and EAs that initially work and then collapse.

At the end of the day in any trading environment, Price Action, Supply & Demand, Momentum are the only winners. Some of the indicators have a higher success rate, but blindly following a "when this line crosses that line and when this bar changes colour " will get you in a hole, unless you take the time and energy to understand what is driving the markets, what the risk is and what the probability is of any particular trade set-up.

The institutional investment organizations control billions of dollars - these are the true market makers, the retail trading market is unlikely to ever have the ability to influence a market - is less coordinated and has much less capital.

OK - I'm off the soap box now. That was my 10 cents on "systems"

Cheers - happy pip hunting.

--- 帖子 #919 ---
Some more hindsight analysis on the EUR/NZD, which can give some huge pip yields if you have the patience.

The Charts are intended as a training exercise so that you can run backtesting and experiment with the add-on approach to maximize the pip yield.

(not sure what happened to Chart #3 in this series - lost in space  )

Chart #1

Further Analysis of EUR/NZD Day Entry

Initial heads up as the up trend stalls and sets a second Fractal with a lower high

Large wick / small body is another heads up on the final white APB

Colour change on APB and a close below the 5EMA gives a first possibility of setting the entry point below the Day low

RSI drops below 50 on the second red candle giving another entry point

Depending on how aggressive your trading style is, this makes a difference of 70 pips

With the 200EMA in play, the conservative entry is to wait until this is broken

Chart #2

As ATR 7 is higher on this pair, you have the option of setting you SL and TP1 to 1XATR7 which in this case is 180pips.  The SL can be set above the previous Day H

TP2 is set to the same SL but with the TP not set (leave at 00000)

Chart #4

TP1 eventually closes at 180 pips after 8 days if you stayed with the initial SL setting.  If you moved the SL to a BE point earlier, this would have closed out, but then you can always re-enter on the next APB colour change.

Once TP1 closes, move SL to BE

Add-On Candles – AOC can be taken any time there is a pause in the trend and the trend resumes and breaks the a resumption and can also be taken on Fractal Breaks

My preference is to wait until TP1 closes before adding on and increasing the exposure.

Chart #5

As you enter each new Add-On, move the SL for each entry to the previous AOC level – this should keep you from being stopped out as the trade pauses/breathes and will protect a large proportion of your profits.

Based on the current price (this would still be an active trade with the SL for all entries moved to AOC5 after AOC6 was entered)

AOC6 =70pips

AOC5 = 220pips

AOC4 = 360pips

AOC3 – 440pips

AOC2 = 590pips

AOC1 = 750pips

Original EP = 930pips

TP1 = 180pips

Best Case Scenario = 3,540pips

Total of 8 entries – TP1, TP2 and the 6 AOC’s over a time period of 32 trading days

Worst case scenario would be that this trade reverses and hits the SL set on AOC5, so the total pip yield would be 2,570.

--- 帖子 #954 ---
Brian,

I use a couple of approaches on SL

In a tighter ranging market I will look to keep around the rule of 1X ATR7, and in a wider ranging market 2xATR7, so this way it ties in with the range moves of the timeframe that you are trading.

Another approach is to use previous swing high/low - which often matches to 2xATR7 rule.

Higher timeframes = larger SL and TP target, with less trades and less time needed on the screen.

the chart shows my thoughts on this trade - if TP1 does not close out in the current candle I would consider closing manually in case the 200ema dynamic support kicks in - TP2 SL would move to BE+20pips and then manually manage any add-ons / profits

Brian,

Depends on whether you let a losing trade run all the way - I have got a lot stricter in pulling the plug on the losers - if it isn't working out, I'll probably kill it on the 3rd candle.

win/lose ratio is pretty high - above 75% and a better measure is pips won / lost which should be 3:1 or better

--- 帖子 #959 ---

--- 帖子 #960 ---
Always wait for the candle to close.  Then ensure that Price Action confirms the move.  I enter in the early stages of the new candle, so for me the new candle starts at 5pm and I enter between 8pm and 9:30 pm, or place pending buy stops or sell stops.

TDI cross should confirm the move along with price action.

I will time my entries off of the old candle H/L which allows Price Action to continue / confirm the move.

If dealing with a fractal based entry, set your entry 5 to 10 pips above / below the fractal.

--- 帖子 #961 ---
Great question.

see the attached chart - not all TDI crosses are created equal, and you can still lose - nothing is foolproof after all, and you do have to pay the forex gods occasionally!

As well as having great angles on the TDI cross, you need good PA momentum with HH / HL, LL / LH, and candles that do not stagnate or pull back / stall

Lord Rothschild has taken a near-£130m bet against the euro as fears continue to grow that the single currency will break up.

The member of the banking dynasty has taken the position through RIT Capital Partners, the £1.9bn investment trust of which he is executive chairman.

The fact that the former investment banker, a senior member of the Rothschild family, has taken such a view will be seen as a further negative for the currency.

The latest omen follows news in The Daily Telegraph late last week that the government of Finland is already preparing for the euro’s break-up.

RIT, which Lord Rothschild has led since 1988, had a -7pc net short position in terms of principal currency exposures on the euro at the end of July, up from -3pc at the end of January. Given a net asset value of £1.836bn at the end of July, the position is worth £128m.

Sources close to RIT suggested that the position was not a dogmatic negative view on the euro as a currency, but rather a realistic approach on a currency that remains relatively weak.

I was not on that one - but my entry point would be the second horizontal line.  I typically like to wait until RSI(10) crosses the 50 - I watch this value in the Data Window.

I only have limited time to post commentary on the charts, so what you see is what you get

For my approach / trading style, once the entry has been executed I only use the H4 to make decisions based on re-entries / SL adjustments, etc.

One of the dangers of dropping to the lower timeframes is that they will often have reached an oversold / overbought area during any trend move on the day charts.

--- 帖子 #1030 ---

--- 帖子 #1031 ---
My trading plan is written based on day charts, so all of my entries are from the day chart.

Once I am in a trade, the only time I go to a lower timeframe is when the PA is stalling.  The H4 charts give me add-on entries, once I am in profit and pips are locked in the bank.

I have no real interest in going lower.  In fact as you go through the lower time frames you will pick up conflicting signals.

The Day will confirm your short entry and show no signs of danger.

The H4 may show a pull back.

M30 will show you a buy signal.

After all of this information what do you do?  Close the trade?  Open a new trade hoping for a reversal?

I decided long ago that I needed a timeframe to stick with and with my lifestyle and available hours, that was the day chart.

It has boiled down to making a choice, sticking with it and having the patience not to be distracted by all of the noise on the lower timeframes.

Most of my trading decisions are based on the day candles (patterns / supply / demand / fractals) and the day RSI 10, so even though the H4 RSI 10 may conflict with the Day RSI 10, I'll usually ignore it, set my SL to a recent H/L and go from there - much more peaceful way of trading - but that's me!

--- 帖子 #1043 ---
When all of the signals are heading in one direction and the Price Action stalls, it can be very powerful to wait for the next move.

Once the PA has paused for several candles look for a Fractal High break as the next re-entry opportunity.

This one gives you over 300pips in a week and if you drop down to the H4 for Add-On Candles, many more are available.

Hope this helps

@ Buttonjock, let me give it a try . . .

suppose E/U is giving a TDI cross at 1.30 and ATR(7) at that moment is 160 pips. The current candle close (ATR(1)) should be 75% of 160 = 120 pips up or down when compared to yesterday's close. In case of an upswing, it should be at 1.30 + 120 pips = 1.3120 .

But let Britpip answer more detailed or precise, he is the one who started this thread and thought out this system, these rules are his brainchild.

--- 帖子 #1076 ---
Greetings all

Been pre-occupied on other stuff but am getting back to trading again in the new year.

Implemented a few tweaks to the overall approach looking at overlaying Supply & Demand - main issue is keeping the charts clean, so very conscious of adding stuff that does not add value.

I have been running with a revision on the TP and SL settings but am still keeping with placing two trades at entry, only now TP1 = 1xATR7 and TP2 = 3xATR7.

Once TP1 is hit, move TP2 to BE and then manage the SL manually.  You also have the option of moving to the H4 to pick up on the Add-Ons as per the training charts.

SL for both trades is 1.5xATR7 OR the previous Fractal, which ever is the lowest value, so if 1.5xATR7 = 150pips and the nearest Fractal is 100pips away from the entry position, then set to a few pips above the Fractal if high, or a few pips lower than the Fractal if low.

I have been manually drawing these for a while now and have found an indicator that does the job well.

Here's the revised template and the new Supply / Demand indicator.

With the new indicator, watch for the PA as it enters a S/D zone - usually it'll lose momentum and then reverse - unless it blows through and breaks the zone!  As it exits a zone, look for an entry point.  Wait for the day candle to close before entering!

--- 帖子 #1091 ---
Hi,

I haven't written anything about the indicator to date - there are a few threads on FF that concentrate on the approach and I'll include these as reference.

here's a quote from Trading Supply & Demand Zones

Sam Seiden (this is a commercial trader, so beware of subscriptions - I do not use his system, but I do credit him with this quote) wrote:

"Noted economist Adam Smith suggested hundreds of years ago that when supply exceeds demand at a price level, prices will decline and vice-versa. Noted physicist Isaac Newton suggested in his three laws of motion that an object will remain in motion until it is met with an equal or greater force. These two simple, yet brilliant principles have stood the test of time and are directly responsible for the movement of price in the markets we trade today. There is no doubt in my mind that the two of them would have made excellent traders."

The general definitions are:

Demand

A price at which someone is willing and able to buy something.

Demand = (Support) = where to buy.

Supply

The price at which someone is willing and able to sell something.

Supply = (Resistance) = where to sell.

Just like any market, the financial markets are a function of supply & demand and good trading opportunities present themselves when this equation is out of balance.

Think of Supply and Demand as the housing market.  When house prices have been running up for some time and reach a certain price point in a geographic area, the prices will often stick there and folks will not pay higher prices, so there is saturation in the housing market and eventually, prices naturally fall.  the supply is exhausted and it becomes a seller's market.  Conversely, when the bottom falls out of the housing market, prices will find a natural low point and it generates demand due to the low prices and it then becomes a buyer's market.

Basic rules are to look for trades entering a zone and wait for the PA to exit the Zone - These will usually coincide with a TDI cross, but this is just another confirmation tool and will help you spot Supply & Demand Zones that are not obvious on your screen without zooming out.  If the Supply / Demand Zone is strong, the end result will be a price reversal.  Weaker Zones will cause the price to stall before resuming its original trend.

Do not enter trades as the PA approaches a Zone - Wait for the bounce / reversal to be confirmed with TDI & PA.

This is a supplemental approach for what I am currently using - I was drawing these boxes anyway, so it is nice to have some software that will do the job reliably.

PhAnTi' has also written some ebooks on the subject - worth a read - chrome://newtabhttp//www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=352479

[quote=Buttonjock;6328273]
The key to demo charts is learning what worked and what didn't.

Go back and review the trades and understand what was happening in the run up to taking the trade and then what happened to to the trade after entry.

Did you follow your trading plan for the entries?

Did you stay in a losing position too long?

Did you exit a winning position too soon?

Some of my losing trades looked appalling when reviewed in the cold light of day!  It hurts even more when it is a live account :-(  However, that is the purpose of conducting a Lessons Learned review and don't forget, keep back testing, keep improving.

Here's to a wonderful 2013

Watch List from close of play Friday.

NFP has had an impact on the charts, but the JPY pairs continue on their merry way.

For any pair that is already trending, try dropping down to the H4 charts to find re-entry possibilities, especially where a new Demand Zone has been established.  Look for entries where PA is leaving the Deamnd Zone - these will usually be confirmed by a TDI recrossing even though it may already be above 68.

EU - Possible resumption of the move south but this will need a move of 90pips + before the previous day low is broken - caution as this heading to a Demand Zone once it clears the 200EMA

GU looks more promising with the Friday doji / spinning top

CHF JPY - Fractal High established - possible pending trade for a fractal break on Day or H4

USD JPY - approaching a Supply Zone - watch for developments during the week

EUR AUD - nice set up for a short re-entry - looks to have stalled on the 200EMA

GBP AUD - has hit a Demand Zone - watching to see if we get a candle reversing off of the zone

AUD CHF - nice set up for a long re-entry - looks to have stalled on the 200EMA

Trading multiple pairs:

This has to be done in accordance with your money / risk management plan otherwise you will blow up your account.   Generally I will trade one pair initially and when that has moved into profit and TP1 is triggered, then I will look for additional pairs.  Base your trading decisions on probability and risk and only take the A+ set-ups.

Happy pip hunting

--- 帖子 #1125 ---
A good example of re-entries on a current trend would be the jpy pairs at present - using the eur/jpy as an example and staying on the day chart would give you 3 clear entries off of Fractal High Breaks.  A really good Re-entry is after PA blows through a new Demand Zone as it did on 12/24 - 12/26 plus it also broke a Fractal High.

Once you have a strong trend as with the eur/jpy - it has been on a run for 20 weeks with a couple of pauses, the RSI will sit way above 51 on the day and then the entries are fairly straightforward.  The week chart shows a strong Demand Zone with the candle exiting and heading north - this coincides with the original day entry point.  This also is a good demonstration of verifying the higher time frames - if the week is on a trend run, then you are only looking for long entries on H4.

The H4 chart makes for much more activity, and again you can use the Fractal High breaks as your entry or as in the Day chart example, as new Demand Zones are established following a pause, enter as the PA heads north again.  There will be more entry opportunities here and a chance to scale into the positions as opposed to most folks taking a larger risk and then scaling out - personal preference!.

For SL on the H4 use the most recent H4 Fractal Low and then follow the trend.

One thing to note here is as you run with the H4 chart for the re-entries, there is more possibility of being stopped out than the day charts, so use the H4 Fractal Low SL settings with caution and allow the trade some breathing room.  This is a great way of stacking up the pips on a strong trend run.

--- 帖子 #1146 ---
Do as I say, not as I do!!!

OK - time to fess up to a bad entry on the day for EUR/AUD.  There are some really good learning points here, so if you follow Rule #1, should keep you out of a bunch of bad entries.  Wait for Day Candle to close and for APB colour change to have been completed.  This means DO NOT enter if you have a series of APBs that are red and the the current day is white.  Wait for the current day to close white.  As PA moves, the colour of the APB will change, so what often looks like a colour change APB, turns into a colour continuation - ask me how I know this.

Rule #2 - If the PA is hovering around the 200EMA, and especially if the 100EMA and 200EMA are running together horizontally and PA is not moving, that is a DO NOT enter signal, as if I haven't known that for an eternity!  This is your signal to go fishing, watch a movie, etc.  If this was ever a pending trade, then it should only have been a sell stop, but seriously, it is still a crap shoot.

At the time of setting the buy stops, TDI was crossing on the Day and had already done so on H4 - Rule #3, wait for day to close and TDI to confirm the cross.

All comments are welcome - on reflection you are never sure why it went wrong - maybe having the week and day red was a clue.

--- 帖子 #1147 ---
Mistakes give you a major kick in the butt that your rules are there for a reason. We've all been down that road, and it never ends well.

Wishing you the best for 2013.

--- 帖子 #1148 ---
I must admit that sometimes we break our own rules. Maybe because we had some success breaking them in the past and thought to ourselves..yea...thats a minor rule. Until it kicks us in the butt!

And of course, there are times when you follow the rules perfectly and still we get kicked in the butt and we wonder why.

In many threads, we see almost the same rules.

1. Buy if abv XX MA or Sell if below x MA

2. Dont trade if you see a MA soup etc etc

All this are really fine advice.

But when we look at the charts....u see great opportunities that are against these rules...so what do we do? Especially for day charts...if you really follow the rules..you end up not trading for 2-3 weeks.

SO, my question is...do you really follow the rule not to Buy when price below a MA, for example a 50MA or 35MA or 100MA??

I think its a SAFE method but ultimately..it limits the frequency of trades.

Just ranting some of the self-argument I have with myself from time to time.

But I think I am learning to just say "NO".

--- 帖子 #1179 ---
GBP/AUD

I still would not rule this out for a run south.  I am waiting for a candle close below the Fractal Low.  TDI well into the 32 zone, so this is a good time to review this pair's history - what does PA generally do when TDI hit 32?  In many cases there is a pause / retrace and then you will see another continuation which can be several hundred pips.  There are also the cases where there is a reversal which holds.

The biggest risk here is a spike lower, breaking the fractal low which ten reverses and becomes a pin bar which triggers your pending short sell stop.

Let the PA confirm this one - TDI is only telling you that it is oversold but there can still be further moves south.

--- 帖子 #1194 ---
Hi piprac.

Not really a magic formulae, mostly based off of Fractals.

My new Day starts at 4pm PDT and I only get to review the charts at 8pm.  If there is a colour change on APB, then I'll look and see where the last Fractal was set - If I like the set up, I'll use the ATR 7 value and set my buy / sell stop about 10% of the ATR 7 value above / below the Fractal.

For example. if the set up is short and the ATR 7 is 100pips, I will set the sell stop 10 pips below the Fractal Low value.

--- 帖子 #1206 ---
WFX,

TP1 / TP2 strategy initially uses the Day ATR 7 to establish TP1 and SL for the entry, so if you have an APB colour change, then take the ATR 7 value for that candle and if it is 90 pips, that is your TP1 setting.  I still use 2XATR 7 or the swing high/low for the SL.

TP2 - two options.

Option 1 - set and forget - set TP2 to 3XATR 7, so if ATR 7 on the set up candle is 90pips, TP2 - 270pips.  Once TP1 is hit move SL for TP2 to BE or run a TS.

Option 2 - manually manage.  Once TP1 is hit move SL for TP2 to BE and then switch to H4 and look for Add-Ons using the H4 Fractals as the entry points together with fresh TDI crosses / bounces.

Lots of training charts posted on this.

--- 帖子 #1211 ---
Fractal Breaks versus TDI Crosses

Time for another good old fashioned hindsight training chart - with a point!

Fractal Breaks can be used very effectively as Add-On entry points, however, using them in conjunction with the TDI Crosses can often keep you out of a losing trade.

Depending on how you manage your entries with your Add-On stop loss settings, a bad entry can stop you out very easily.

EUR JPY is a good example and shows several Day Chart Fractal High Breaks.  Check out the strength / non existence of a TDI Cross with these breaks.  The weaker the TDI Cross, the more risk of a Draw Down and a busted trade as your stop loss is hit and then the trade continues its trend - very frustrating and to a point avoidable.

Only two options with the Day Charts:

Option 1 - set your SL at 2XATR 7 from the Fractal High candle

Option 2 - wait for a strong TDI Cross to coincide with a Fractal High Break - do not jump the gun and enter early (ask me how I know this)

--- 帖子 #1212 ---
Now that the II_SupDem has deleted the Supply Zone, does not mean that it is still not an applicable area of concern (it is just the way the software works for this indicator) - just manually insert it and watch for PA to either continue the trend on H4 which will generate a Fractal High Break AND give a new TDI Cross which will confirm the move.

OR, watch for the reversal signals.

This is where common sense and PA overrides an indicator.  Software is only capable of so much, and PA doesn't care what the code says

One of the TDI patterns that gives really good reversals is when the RSI Price Line & Trade Signal Lines pull away from the Mid Zone Line and especially when this occurs in the Overbought / Oversold areas.

Combine this with a Supply / Demand Zone and the PA moves can be quite dramatic.

--- 帖子 #1261 ---
Some thoughts on APB Colour Changes and what to look for with regard mostly to reversals but can also apply after a consolidation period followed by a trend continuation.

Guidelines Summary.

1. Wait for day candle to close

2. Confirm Colour Change - set entries slightly above candle high for longs, below candle low for shorts

3. Best colour change candles have wicks top and bottom - usually top and bottom wicks will be similar in value, although not essential - also, they will have more body than wicks, again not essential

4. Colour change candle value (ATR 1) should be at least 75% of the previous candle ATR 7

5. Colour change candles that are > 2X of the ATR7 may result in a PA stall - can still be valid entries, but may not produce +ve results straight away

6. TDI crosses that coincide with a colour change candle are great, especially if the TDI is in Overbought / Oversold territory

7. Watch for candle reversal patterns preceding a colour change such as doji / hammer / shooting star / inside candle / engulfing candle - these all improve yor success probability

8. Colour change candles closing and moving away from a Supply / Demand Zone are also really strong indicators

Look for these patterns when backtesting and verify what patterns work best for your trading plan / style.

Standard entry rules apply - use the colour change candle ATR 7 - set TP1 to 1 X ATR 7 - SL can be Swing high / low or 1.5 to 2 X ATR 7.  Set TP2 with the same SL and leave TP open - move to BE when TP1 is hit and then change to H4 and manage SL manually and look for H4 Add-Ons on Fractal Breaks.

This has been added as a reference post to Post #1

--- 帖子 #1303 ---
Hey all,

Just adding what I found as some interesting observations on the eurusd with Fibonacci's.

The first chart is a long term look with a couple of fibs in gray on significant highs and lows. The second chart is our standard view with a couple of short term fibs added in brown.

What we are looking at is not the individual lines but the groupings of the older and newer.

About now at 1.3050 both the short fibs have lines that align very tightly with an older fib. If you zoom out this will also show as a significant pivot point several times; since setpt/12 feb-may/12, Dec/10 to jan/11 and several others even as far back as 1991. It also just happens to be the level of our 200 EMA at the moment.

There's also a looser grouping around 1.2880 that aligns with a demand zone.

Shorter term, 1.331 and 1.265 have significant groupings.

What I'm suggesting is, we may see price movement for a while around the first two fibs with extensions to the higher and lower points and back.

Comments anyone?

Cheers

--- 帖子 #1321 ---
Thanks, good to know and glad at least someone missed this pahlava of a trade

A little something on NFP from Wikipedia. I'd assumed it was always the first Friday. Apparently not.

"The Bureau of Labor Statistics releases preliminary data on the third Friday after the conclusion of the reference week, i.e., the week which includes the 12th of the month, at 8:30 a.m. Eastern Time; typically this date occurs on the first Friday of the month." (but not always ...!)

--- 帖子 #1322 ---
This caught a lot of experienced traders out this week - showing you just how important it is to be aware of the key news events.

For each currency, this is usually the equivalent of NFP - typically unemployment / employment numbers.  Canada releases theirs usually on the same day as the USA.  Others vary.

The other key one for USA to note is the FOMC.

--- 帖子 #1333 ---
Mine is the TMS Watchdog version posted here on 12/11/2011 and I have always had the bands visible.

If you go into the Indicator settings for TDI, lines 1 and 3 are the upper and lower bands.

If you go to Dean Malone's website, one of the trade signals he teaches is breaks of the bands.  Buy when the upper band is broken on an up trend and sell when the lower band is broken on a down trend.  Well, that's the simple version - more detail can be found by watching his training videos.

--- 帖子 #1363 ---
After several recent chart sessions, it becomes clear that the charts do actually speak volumes.

Here is an example where the TDI signal and RSI lines have pulled away from the mid zone and PA has pushed away from the EMA21.  Typically this results in a PA stall as we are seeing now on this pair and then a retrace for the TDI back to the mid zone, especially when it is running under the 50 level.  This will also reult in PA pulling back to the EMA21.

Worth a more serious look at the history of TDI patterns and PA pulling away from EMA21 to see how reliable it is.  One thing to note is that when TDI signal and RSI lines have pulled away and rreach into OB / OS territory, the pullback is stronger.

Another observation is that when the TDI mid zone line is running at the 32 / 68 levels, there is a very good chance of a strong reversal move, especially Day and H4 charts.

Hey,

--- 帖子 #1413 ---
TDI thoughts and observations.

Generally, the TDI Mid Zone / Trade base line (blue) likes to be around the 50 level.  If it strays to the 32 / 68 zones, or even breaks through these zones, then PA will very likely reverse.

Any time the TDI Trade Signal Line and the RSI Price Line break the 32 . 68 levels, watch for reversals.

The Trade Signal line also gives some clues on where PA is heading.  the attached chart shows horizontal sky blue lines to highlight the Trade Signal Line reversing.

It is not normal to have a strong TDI entry signal if the cross goes against the direction of the Trade Signal Line.  What this means is that when the Trade Signal Line is heading down and the RSI Price Line crosses and heads up, this is probably not going to be supported by PA,

Notice how the Trade Signal Line flattens out after a trend run and once there is an APB colour change, the PA will confirm the TDI Cross.  Wait for the second candle to confirm the PA and wait for the Trade Signal Line to confirm the direction and you will have stronger entries.  Just for fun, I expanded the Indicator Window 2 to really show how this looks.

We are always looking for the silver bullet to get in earlier, however, if you can increase the probability of a successful trade entry but you have to give up 10 or 20 pips to do so, would you?

Anyway, here's another brilliant hindsight training chart that may show you how it should look - now ll you have to do is make it work on a live chart!

For back testing, use the 1 X ATR7 value for your TP1 and see how many times it is hit for your favourite pair.  Then see what happens if you use 2XATR7 for TP2.  Play with the values and keep lots of notes / spreadsheets.  Build you stats and figure out your probability of success for the settings.

Happy pip hunting

--- 帖子 #1422 ---
Following on from posts regarding the TDI Trade Signal Line and allowing it to flatten or reverse so that when the TDI cross occurs the Trade Signal Line is heading in the same direction as PA, here's an H4 chart for review.

Because the TDI cross occurs before the APB Colour change, the entry point could be taken early, or wait until PA confirms.  As this is H4, there are multiple Add-On opportunities.

With H4 trades, I will often use the ATR 7 setting from the Day chart for TP1, so this would yield 60 pips for TP1 and TP2 plus add-ons would give you over 400pips to date.

A good example of an H4 entry followed by add-ons for pip farming

--- 帖子 #1431 ---
AG,

Waiting for the A+ set-ups is what makes the difference, so, essentially not placing trades and hoping they work out.  Wait for PA to really confirm the move and if you are using indicators or patterns including supply and demand zones, wait for the previous candle (set up candle) to close and then either at the end of the candle or at the beginning of the new candle make your decisions.

I am placing less trades with waiting for the move to confirm, but see better results.

I would avoid the approach that increases risk - I want to see safe and boring trades.  The GU training chart that I posted was a high probability low risk trade - this is what I look for to increase my pip yields.  Managing your trades once they are in profit and giving your trades space to breathe will help as will cutting the losing trades after it is clear that the PA is not following your rules.

The two biggest reasons for traders not making profits are:

1. Cutting a profitable trade too early

2. Keeping a losing trade running for too long and hoping it will turn around (this is probably the hardest skill to perfect because nobody likes losing!!!).

--- 帖子 #1440 ---
Greetings All,

Been playing around with TDI and seeing what would be possible with a single screen MA approach and de-cluttering the screen.  Always looking at options for simplifying the data and the entry criteria.

This closely replicates what the TDI does with the benefit of keeping everything on the main chart - I do have RSI as a second window open for posting the RSI value in my Data screen, so displaying it as a chart is optional, but sort of defeats the objective of the single screen approach -you can always compress it -  may work better as a displayed chart on the lower timeframes.

If you backtest, always disable the fractals and be aware that the overall trend of the MAs once set are influenced by where the next candle went, so an F12 test gives you a good idea, but live testing will give different results - personally I prefer looking at the screen to see how to differentiate between good entry signals and ones that stalled out / failed.

The MA crosses are very close to the TDI - usually same candle and does on occasion filter out false TDI crosses, so worth a live experiment for forward testing - you can always add in the TDI to compare as you test.

Looking to continue with the adapted TDI rule where the slower MA has to flatten out and adopt the same direction as the PA - slightly slower entry criteria, but has more probability of success.  Looks good on Day and H4, but that would be as low as I would go on timeframes.

The usual rules on the 100/200EMAs apply - see Post #1 - also on candle patterns - engulfing / inside bar / pull back / pin bar / shooting star / hammer, all help support the entry criteria

the arrows are taken from an indicator that I think came from Lawgirl's threads and has been modified for this approach - these are more of a head's up indicator and to verify the pattern / slope of the slow MA and PA.  When you see multiple arrows of the same colour, this usually results in a move in the direction indicated.  Everything else is from my original charts.

for RSI 10, I am using <49 for shorts and >51 for longs, unless the Day entry is really strong - RSI will lag especially on the Day.

The attached chart is H1 which shows RSI 10 as a valid signal to confirm entries - so with the example on H1, each valid entry and 2 entry positions, would have yielded a total of over 200 pips over a 10 period when PA was pretty much range trading, so trading H1 and M15 is always an option in these conditions

--- 帖子 #1445 ---
Interpreting the APB colour changes on Day can be challenging.

On the current GU, we have had several single day colour changes - here's how I am looking at them.

First of all, when monitoring the day charts, I will see the colour change at the end of the day, so this means that PA changed during the previous day and changed the colour, so dropping down to H4 and in some cases H1 and looking for confirmation helps me to verify what PA is doing for the next couple of candles.  This will be the start of the Asian session, so can be pretty quiet, but is worth doing.

PA breaks of the Asian channel can be very productive, but follow the major trend unless you are scalping the pause / pull back

The H4 chart also gives you Add-On options when you see a new MA cross

--- 帖子 #1486 ---
For those of us eagerly awaiting the reversals of the AUD based currencies, bear in mind the link to gold.  AUD is a commodity based currency and closely follows gold.  CAD does a similar thing with oil.

Gold has had a long run up and was fueled in part by world economies faltering.  As these economies recovered, gold lost its appeal.  So, for AUD to reverse, gold needs to have some strength.  Maybe G8 and FOMC may shed some light on the directions, but PA is still key.

AUD could just as easily continue recent trend runs.  Wait for clear breaks of current ranges and keep your money management tight.

Hi David,

Reminds me of years ago when the McClellans talked about waiting for a buy spike on their oscillator when trading equities. Takes lots of patience for the longer trends. Even a solid TDI cross on the Weekly usually needs to prove itself with continuing strong separation as RSI and the Signal cross through 50. Frequently I see that to be the best entry configuration with the highest likelihood for multiple add-ons. Even more so if this is preceeded by a period of low volatility in proximity to the 200 MA. I know, lots of requirements, but the payoff can be huge even if only a few times a year.

Best, AG

--- 帖子 #1577 ---
I now focus on 12 pairs and have these on 12 up charts for PA and TDI - I have these set up in Profles and have them set for Day / H4 and H1.

It's easy to set up - go to profiles and click on Default.

Create a chart and save it as a template - right click and go to Template and Save Template.

Open 12 new charts for the pairs you trade - doesn't have to be 12 - your choice - and set them up from your template folder to the chart set up that you use and then go to Window and click Tile Vertically.  then save the profile.

You can scan the day and h4 profiles for TDI activity / crosses, then go to the PA profile and then click on the pair that has crossed and trade away.

Hi David,

I am a big fan of this approach but because I am looking for the longer term Trends, I add the Weekly TF for a bigger picture view. I also smooth the HA candles, n=2, for starker contrasts. The best Trends will then be a bit easier to spot with persistent color change, growing candles and the absence of near side wicks. The reappearance of near side wicks can be a clue that time may be growing short for the Trend long before a color change. I hope that you do not mind, but I have enclosed an example.

--- 帖子 #1584 ---
If you use these 2 SCRIPTS you don't have to change Profiles, just change the time frame with a few clicks, then change the Template with a few more clicks

It helps if your Templates are on top of the list, the Scripts count from Zero - 0, so if your Template is at the very top, no need to enter a number when it is run

Time frame is the usual MT4 convention in minutes, eg 15, 60, 240, 1440

Hope that helps someone

--- 帖子 #1599 ---
From onlinetradingconcepts.com

The Hanging Man candlestick formation, as one could predict from the name, is a bearish sign. This pattern occurs mainly at the top of uptrends and is a warning of a potential reversal downward. It is important to emphasize that the Hanging Man pattern is a warning of potential price change, not a signal, in and of itself, to go short.
http://www.onlinetradingconcepts.com...gingManPic.gif
The Hanging Man formation, just like theHammer, is created when the open, high, and close are roughly the same price. Also, there is a long lower shadow, which should be at least twice the length of the real body.
When the high and the open are the same, a bearish Hanging Man candlestick is formed and it is considered a stronger bearish sign than when the high and close are the same, forming a bullish Hanging Man (the bullish Hanging Man is still bearish, just less so because the day closed with gains).
After a long uptrend, the formation of a Hanging Man is bearish because prices hesitated by dropping significantly during the day. Granted, buyers came back into the stock, future, or currency and pushed price back near the open, but the fact that prices were able to fall significantly shows that bears are testing the resolve of the bulls. What happens on the next day after the Hanging Man pattern is what gives traders an idea as to whether or not prices will go higher or lower.

--- 帖子 #1630 ---
After testing a variety of formats, I am keeping the TDI on the chart because it does give some good confirmations which you may otherwise miss.

TDI is an overlay onto a MACD which is there as a general momentum indicator - The OSMA Oscillator is very similar, and the Awesome Oscillator is also good - but pick one and go with it.

The RSI may be too much on top of all of this, but knowing the value is a good thing.

All the rules are intact, so no changes there.  The colours work for me with my colour vision issues, so feel free to make it work for you.

The main chart has lost the Supply and Demand Zones because mostly they were sitting on the primary Weekly S/R price lines, so once you zoom out and fix them, they will not repaint as the zones do when PA hits them.

The White arrows are the 2/7 EMA confirmation and I am currently testing with the Black arrows which are 5/10 EMA confirmations - they may not add anything, so could well get nuked in the next version.

So no need to add any wierd indicators - Big E would be non too impressed by the additions, but they seem to help - it's all a personal choice at the end of the day.

Happy pip hunting

--- 帖子 #1641 ---
Here is a great example for what NFP can do to what would appear to be a great set up.

Trading before NFP is like rolling the dice - you have no idea what will happen, so if you like your odds at 50/50 then go place all your money on black and go to Vegas.

This example, depending on how you placed your trade - pending as a sell stop or a by market sell, would either have not triggered if you set your Entry Point below the Thursday Low, or you would be sitting 190pips if placed as a sell by market.

As Nancy Reagan would say - Just say No to placing trades before NFP - same advice applies to FOMC news events!

Happy pip hunting

--- 帖子 #1667 ---
Expanding a bit on the Weekly Reversals observation.

When the Weekly candles show an engulfing pattern, this is a heads up that the trend has a high probability of reversing.

The stronger the initial engulfing candle, the higher the probability of success, so if the engulfing candle pattern is achieved with one candle, this is stronger than a reversal patterns that takes two candles to achieve the full cover of the previous candle.

These weekly / engulfing reversal patterns look to precede any TDI Cross confirmation and as for the 2/7EMA, this may also come too late on the live charts - looks encouraging on this chart, but not sure how far into the week it triggers - just there as an information point at this time and one to watch for live / forward testing.

As usual, this is work in progress going forward - may be useful to back test this as it is just candle patterns and no indicators involved (remove the fractals and the 2/7 arrows for back testing), but definitely worth bearing in mind that the Weekly chart always drives the momentum and probability of the day chart move.

Time to analyze a trade that is actually in process as opposed to completed trades or hindsight training charts.

EA Weekly Chart was on a very strong up trend, however, MACD is showing a strong bearish divergence and TDI has flattened, so technically a Bearish signal. especially being heavily oversold,

EA Day Chart was showing the initial PA running out of steam with MACD, RSI 10 and TDI RSI Price Line all rolling over on the last 2 white APB candles.  TDI Trade Signal Line has nicely rolled over, making a TDI cross very strong for the reversal.  TDI is then supporting the PA move.

Once the APB colour change candle closes, you have a potential Entry Point - this would have caught the Entry Point #2 on the H4 Chart.  This Entry Point would have triggered on the 3rd black APB candle.

The 2/7EMA confirmation arrow appears after the close of the 3rd black APB candle, so this provides another entry signal.

EA H4 chart shows how to look at PA when the Day Chart is giving an indication of a move and then starts to roll over.

The H4 chart was showing TDI Bearish Divergence against the PA, so the set up is there several candles before the first TDI cross and well in advance of the signals on the Day chart.  Entry Point #1 as it turned out was not a strong running one as it initially went for 110pips and then suffered a 55pip drawdown before Entry Point 2 was confirmed with the TDI Cross and a Fractal Low break.  This time the PA move is stronger until it takes a four candle rest (go to YouTube and watch "four candles" by the two Ronnies - hilarious) and then resumes the trend for Entry Position 3, which is the one that I am riding.

For additional Add-Ons, watch this on H4 or H1, but for my trade, it will depend on how much gap we see on Sunday, especially as I only have 20 pips left from my trailing stop of 65pips - maybe I should have closed the trade before Friday close, but with 100pips locked in, I'm prepare to risk 65 for a longer trade run and Add-Ons.

Happy pip hunting

--- 帖子 #1693 ---
Trade Summary for the week.

13 trades set up for pending trades (buy stops / sell stop) which is a really high number of trades in a week for me.

10 trades triggered (including one oops with a sell by market instead of a pending sell stop - don't ask - which was immediately closed so that I stick to the trading plan!)

9 profits and 1 loss (including a couple of BE stop outs after the trades were in profit), this includes the current trade with 100pips locked in.

Pips won 32/99/4(BE)/68/29/2(BE)/18/18/100 = 370

Pips lost 3(oops trade - sell by market) = 3

Win to Loss Ratio 370/3 which is not bad

This is my best ever win/loss ratio since going live (and I would have to say is an exceptional result - certainly not typical), so we shall see how this pans out over the next few weeks.  I spend about 2 hours per day analyzing and placing the set ups and closing the trades.  These were all pending trades that triggered while I was sleeping and then the closure is one of 4 scenarios:

a) hit TP target

b) closed when I woke up

c) closed after setting to run with TS

d) closed later in the day on a pull back / PA stall

Just to confirm, this is a live account and the current lot size is 0.02, so $20 per trade.  Risk per trade is below 5% and they key is to watch your total exposure when trading multiple pairs. Same rules apply when you start adding on to winning positions - understand how many trades you are opening and what your total risk is.

It may look really impressive in a demo account having 20+ trades open, but if you get a bad news result / central bank announcement / natural disaster - earthquake, then all those pending pips will reverse on you.  No harm in the demo, but do this with real money and there will be tears - ask me how I know this

If JPY is on a trend run, then pick 2 of the strongest pairs - same with any of the currencies, otherwise you will risk over trading and blow your account.

Happy pip hunting - looking forward to next week

--- 帖子 #1707 ---
Quieter week this week on the trading front due to a heavier work schedule, so little time to focus - ended up 60 pips down for the week due to closing two trades too early - each would have gone on to hit their respective TPs.

A comment from another thread by claudia1 would be worth understanding.

She wrote in response to the question - What's the win rate thus far?

"Win rate is irrelevant its how you manage the trades is what its all about. Can lose 70% of trades and still be in profit. to answer your question i do win 70% of trades manually at around one to to one risk reward."

This is a typical FF question from folks trawling through threads looking for the silver bullet / holy grail.

To expand a tad more on this.  If you trade for an institution, no one cares about your win rate.  If your win rate is 70% but you end up with some real stinkers that kill your account, what good was the win rate?  Claudia1's point is well made and you should concentrate on minimizing your risk in order to maximize your profits.  Understand what your A+ entry conditions are and follow your plan.

A better measurement is $ won versus $ lost, or % gain in the account, etc.

Phx62 has made similar comments when asked these types of questions and points out that no two individuals trade the same, so knowing one person's results, although gratifying, is actually of little use.  All it will tell you is whether a trader is consistent in their approach and disciplined in their following their trading plans and money management plans.

--- 帖子 #1733 ---
1- Which trend do you follow: Daily, weekly, or monthly? or what combination of trends that must line up to trade? [e.g. daily and weekly!] I use the weekly for S/R levels as well as overall trend - sometimes you will have pullbacks on the day chart that are tradeable, but all my entry signals are form the day charts.

2- What should I do when price for no reason stalls? once you lose your initial trade entry signals, all bets are off and it is a 50/50 call - best bet, cancel and start again - look for new entry positions

3- Is there any way to know whether the price is going to breach the supp and demand zones or not! not really - PA is king and it will tell you where it wants to go - no predictive indicators I'm afraid.

4- Do you keep the trade going when it reaches these zones?  If you have two trades running you can close one and manage the second - I am inclined to close and wait for the next signal.

--- 帖子 #1735 ---
For noobs like myself:

1- Trust the system if it makes sense and try to follow it. Don't break your own rules!

2- Give the price room to breathe. All the trades I lost wasn't because of the system, but because I closed it immediately when the price started ranging away from it's predicted direction.. But the next day I found it booming in my favor after I closed the trade. Or because I put a small SL range!

3- If you're using TMS hist indicator, I found that when Daily trend is up and gave you a signal, but W & MN are down, it might be a lazy or short movement like what is happening now in EUR/USD [The only exception is when the PA is bouncing off of a supply and demand zones or S/R levels [including 200ema].

--- 帖子 #1747 ---
This is where opening two trades per entry will help.

TP1 = 1 X ATR 7

TP2 - leave to run - move to BE after TP1 is hit and then manage / add-on as appropriate.

Currently EUR/CAD day PA is approaching a Supply Zone, so may not be a great example, however, following the two trades theory, with my current trades - TP1 would have closed out for 130pips, leaving TP2 to run which is currently at 200pips with an add-on.

For SL settings once a trend run has been established and the Day candles have stayed above the EMA7 for a few days, I will often use the H4 Fractals (Fractal Lows for the up trend), or previous Day Low to track the trend.

Once the H4 moves above the 68 level, I will normally wait for a pause / mini retrace before a new add-on, of for PA to break a Fractal high.

If the H4 PA starts to close below the H4 EMA 7, this is a heads up that consolidation / pull back is coming, so manage accordingly.

--- 帖子 #1757 ---
Sometimes it holds on to the text label

This may take a few steps, but first step is to set the TDI text settings to false and see if that removes the erroneous text.

You can also go into the screen objects and highlight each of the text labels and delete.

Then, if you want the text back, go back into the TDI settings and reset to True

--- 帖子 #1765 ---
Mr Brit, allow me to address noobs like my self again:

After massive backtesting, I can tell you hints:

If you're lost and can't keep up analyzing charts like Mr Brit, and you can't even achieve profits like his, you can stick to some basic rules:

1- Show the market base line [the yellow line] in your TDI and add level [50]. Buy when ever both green and red line are above yellow line and level 50 and the opposite for short positions. [this will protect you from trading against the overall trend, because the yellow line represents the trend]

2- Pay good attention to divergence [regular and hidden] if an uptrend is making higher highs and TDI is making lower highs, you don't need to wait TDI to cross level 50 and market base line, enter the trade as soon as TDI crossover occurs.

3- Money management is the most important thing. If you chose to apply these conservative conditions for trading, you can divide your trades by Targeting more than 2 or 3 TP starting by [0.5XATR] then [1XATR}...etc

4- I don't stick to 2% trades, I always use mini lots in my 1K account.

5- You'll get 2 or 3 conservative trades for each pair / month. If you're trading mini lots.. do the math.

6- Stick to daily charts and avoid keeping open trades during the weekend [because of the gaps].

8- Don't trade any pair on demo or live before doing manual backtesting for it [usually I do the backtesting using LHF simulator for a whole year]

These rules are very conservative with moderate but guaranteed profits till you gain confidence in this trading style, then you can improvise like Mr. Brit.

Mourad

Egypt

--- 帖子 #1767 ---
It is worth noting here that the M15 can be traded within the overall trends / retraces, so this means trading counter to the Day / week, so if we are running with a long on the day, US brokers will not allow a short - no hedging.

For those of us that can trade the M15 and the day, you will need two accounts in the USA so that you can run with the longer term trades and then pick up the pauses / pull backs.

For those of us that do not have that luxury, then it is much simpler - trade the Day / H4 and sleep well

--- 帖子 #1773 ---
Following on from the current PA on GU and touching on some comments on the TMS thread, the GU has a large Master Candle at the moment of 270 pips.

Additionally PA is sitting underneath a Day Supply Zone and a Weekly S/R level.

These candles can be traded in a couple of ways - first with regards to the day charts, treat them as an Inside Candle set up and wait for the breakout, second, drop down to the lower timeframes.  Once the second day candle does not break the H/L, then it is a reasonable move to drop down and trade the range, and in many cases this will result in hitting the breakout move when it finally appears.

Here's the Day Master Candle and the resulting H1 chart

Hi Brit

Just wondering what it is you look for the day MACD to be doing for trend confirmation? Thanks

--- 帖子 #1836 ---
I generally will not take trades against the MACD direction.

Once MACD flattens or starts to pull back, that is usually a sign of consolidation - typically it will coincide with Day PA reaching a weekly S/R region of a Supply / Demand Zone.

If the MACD resumes, then the trend is continuing and look for new entries.

--- 帖子 #1841 ---
For the CCI 14, I am testing it with the MACD.

Currently the initial results seem to support the theory that when MACD is stalling on a long position and then starts to decrease, CCI will reduce and cross the +100.  This is an early warning of price reversal and time to either close the long positions or at least bring the SL up to most recent H4 Fractal Low.  There are occasions where this will only result in a price stall and then consolidation.  EU is looking promising - hence the pending short sell.

Opposite for Short positions

Blue line on H4 is EMA7 - Simple - typical - shift 0

Same for the Day except shift of 1

--- 帖子 #1849 ---
when you are all done with your chart analysis, it is always fun to read the news.  See how the MS viewpoint compares with your analysis - but then realize that they are betting on both sides of the coin here with their short term long and their medium term short!

Morgan Stanley reversed its bets on EUR/USD in its short-term macro portfolio from short to long. MS exited its EUR/USD long from 1.3800 on a small profit and entered long from 1.3730, with a stop at 1.3660, and a target at 1.3950.
"EURUSD is set to keep the pressure on the upside, we believe, as year-end related factors are likely to remain EUR supportive. Hence, we enter near-term tactical bullish strategy as repatriation-related flows drive currencies further away from fundamental and market-orientated indicators. We expect the 1.3830 highs of the year (achieved in October) to be tested, with a move above here opening the way for gains towards our near-term 1.3950 target," MS says as a rationale behind this call
"However, we maintain our medium-term bearish view and would look to re-establish bearish strategies in this area," MS adds outlining its EUR/USD medium-term strategy.
In line with this view, MS maintains a short EUR/USD position in its medium-term macro portfolio from 1.36 (target 1.27, stop 1.3830).

All open trades have been closed as everything has slowed down significantly which means any signals that were in play are now waiting for the next push, so I will sit to the side and see where they go.

While everything has slowed down it gives us a chance to relax and have some screen time without distractions of trading.  When I set my charts up I always add on the Weekly S/R levels from the historical levels.

To do this I start off with just the main chart window, so all other indicator windows have been switched off by using the indicator properties window and by deselecting the weekly timeframe to leave yourself with candles.  From that point add horizontal lines at the significant reversal levels - I use the Weekly Close.  I will often add text to each level so that I can refer to it later.  One thing that will often happen is that a Weekly S/R level will occur at a Big Round Number, which is often cited as a "psychological level" for traders (possibly self fulfilling prophesies!).  Sometimes instead of a definitive price point, there will be a zone which can be up to 100 pips.

These stay on you charts as you drop to the lower timeframes so long as you click on the object after it is created - depending on your settings for options of course and this can be changed by selecting Tools and then Options and then Objects.

I find that this helps with a certain level of prediction for PA losing momentum as it reaches these levels, so either exiting trades as PA closes in on an S/R level or managing with tighter stop losses are options.

Common moves at these levels are consolidation / bounces and reversals.

--- 帖子 #1864 ---
Measures for success on your trading plans

Do Not worry too much about your overall Profit Trades as a % of total - you may have lots of B/E or small profit trades which will skew the stats.

Do worry about the following:

Gross Profit = total $ won

Gross Loss = total $ lost

Total Net Profit = Gross Profit minus Gross Loss

Profit Factor = Gross Profit divided by Gross Loss - this is the number to focus on.  To get this number higher, set yourself goals on each trade and rules as to how many pips you are prepared to give up on a winning trade (trailing stops, cave manager, etc?), as well as SL settings and how you manage losing trades (once a trade goes against you, how many pips are you willing to lose?).

Here's my final numbers for December - very pleased with the month as I often have other commitments in my schedule which conflict with trading every day. Only 17 trades and only trading with 0.02 lots = $20 per trade.  Depending on your account size and risk management, this level of trading can be a good supplement to your income, so if you trade with 0.1 lots, your income multiplies by 5, and so on!

Maybe that's the New Year resolution - trade on a more consistent basis with larger volumes - we shall see

Happy pip hunting on 2014 - may all your pips be green

--- 帖子 #1937 ---
Looking more at the candle patterns and especially patterns that repeat.

After a strong week, the Friday candle sets HH / HL and a Higher close, which also closes out the week at a recent high

Sunday can either show a small gain or loss, but the Monday candle engulfs Sunday with Tuesday confirming the PA move.

The full chart shows the indicators in play, and if you zoom out again you will see that this price point has been hot as a closing price on 5 occasions, so a pretty good resistance level

The candles on their own tell you a story - adding indicators can reinforce the opinion - some times!!!

--- 帖子 #1938 ---
Looking for Support and Resistance Levels

Once you have set this up on each chart, it takes a minimal amount of time to maintain - at the end of each week review the chart and see if there is any justification for moving levels / adding new levels.

Chart 1 - start with a blank chart on candlesticks and go to the weekly chart for the pair you are setting up and zoom all the way out - this chart is GU

Chart 2 - switch to Line Chart and look for key prices where you see pull backs / stalls - Use the crosshair to check  for multiple price points - the more times the price level is hit, the stronger the S / R level - add Horizontal Lines and depending on your preference, either choose a thicker line or a particular colour for the strongest levels / Historic High / Low.  Big Round Numbers (BRNs) also often make for stalling points for PA.  0.5000 1.0000 1.5000 2.0000, etc and often 0.750 1.2500 1.7500, etc  The BRNs can be a different colour.  At this stage don't put too many lines otherwise everything becomes an s/r level and it will bee too confusing.

Chart 3 - start to zoom in and revert to candlesticks and verify / fine tune your levels.  On the weekly chart I will look to put levels at reversals / candlestick closes.

Chart 4 - zoom in one more time and finalize your fine tuning

Chart 5 - switch back to the day chart and you should be set up to show the weekly supprt and resistance levels along with you standard indicators

--- 帖子 #1942 ---
The weekly S and R levels are very powerful and reversal patterns will form around these levels.

Engulfing Candles bouncing off a S/R level is often a strong signal as is a Pin Bar and Pull Backs with large shadows

--- 帖子 #1943 ---
Introducing ema's into the charts can provide visibility of "Dynamic S and R Levels" as PA hits key emas and bounces away.

The 89ema is often key on the Day chart as is the 200ema

An EMA cross of the 7ema and 23ema can lead to a reversal / trend confirmation

Strong trend runs will often use the 50ema as a dynamic level.

All emas are simple with price = typical hlc/3, shift zero apart from the 7ema which has a shift of 1

--- 帖子 #1959 ---
Reading indicators and understanding what they are telling you can give you an edge with your trading

All indicators are based off of averages, which means they are all lagging indicators.  I have yet to see a leading indicator.  Many candle patterns are touted as being high probability reversal signals but you can read PA in accordance with the indicators, regardless of whether it is MACD / Stochastics / Awesome Oscillator, etc.

With this indicator, I would be looking to secure my positions and maybe close all open positions.  This is the Bill Williams - Awesome Oscillator and it is saying that PA momentum is drying up.  If PA stalls at this level, the indicator will change colour, and if PA then continues the trend, another white bar will be set and this is a good re-entry or add-on signal

--- 帖子 #1960 ---
Some random thoughts from Big E on trade entries - he was referring to H4 charts for these comments - HA refers to Heikin Ashi - we are using APB, very similar behaviour.  These are from the first 5 pages of the Trading Made Simple forum and well worth going back and re-reading the early days when Big E was active and posting training charts.

TDI was his only indicator although he did start out with Stochastics for confirmation and later dropped them.  On the main chart he had a 5EMA with a shift of 1 or 2 to show general PA.  So this can be done without all the crap I put on the charts - start simple and see where it takes you.

Hope this helps a few of you in being convinced that the H4 and Day charts offer much less stress and much higher returns for your efforts and to believe that more indicators don't really help   Thanks to Big E - he'll always be remembered on these threads

HA candles average a 3-8 candle run in most cases when it reverses... That's why I want to enter on candle 1 or 2 if I see a set up. A single candle on the 4hr nets you 30-60 pips or more generally. If it goes 3-4 candles you've already made 80-150 pips.

A set up is NOT GREEN TOUCHING RED. Why? Many times green bounces back and the original direction continues. That's a bounce trade.
Wait for green to CROSS RED and open your trade at the beginning of the new candle... usually candle 1 or 2.
Catch the momentum...

A Normal entry is when green crosses red on the TDI (and you can actually see the green on the other side)
A bounce trade is when green gets close to red but bounces away and the original trade continues are good entries generally.
I always look to the left for a possible res/sup level being near. If it's close I pass on the trade and go find another...

I generally quit trading at 6am Pacific (9am est). Why? The market might cook some for the next hour or two but unless there is a hot news announcement during the day... the market pretty much peters out and ranges... I don't want to be trading in that junk. Thats where dealers make most of your money is ranging markets and 5-15 min time frame trading... you got to quit trading those trash time frames. Granted there are 2 out of 100 who can Kick bootie there but chances are your in the 98% who can't. I hear it over and over traders complaining that they have 2-3 years experience but can't keep their head above water... always losing or just breaking even... or worse...

You can't get different results if you keep doing the same thing over and over... just ain't gonna happen anytime soon...

Years ago I traded stocks but later switched to fx. I started using higher timeframes moving up from 5 to 15 to 30 to 1hr and I was seeing benefits every time I went higher. Kept working on the TDI honeing it to the maximum simplicity possible and moving up to 4hr charts and trading at my bed time... wow what a difference in pips earned... stress free as I slept...

--- 帖子 #1986 ---
The indicators that help me the most on day charts are the support / resistance levels.  The weekly S/R levels are often stall points / reversal points as well as the 200ema which becomes a dynamic S/R level.  The Supply / Demand Zones are part of this and they often coincide with the weekly S/R levels.

PA leaving or bouncing off of these is often a strong entry point and in many cases precedes the TDI cross.  Moving average crossovers do work for some folks, but are usually read in partnership with other indicators and this adds to the data points in making decisions and often to the analysis paralysis syndrome.

The APB colour change is an additional bonus for an entry as once the colour changes (with a decent candle body and smaller wicks, or a pin bar) the PA will usually follow that direction for several candles.

Waiting until EOD gives you some time to review / analyze the PA relative to the indicators, or the recent candle patterns and in many cases the Asia session can kick off a new move.  At the very least, you can create a watch list for pairs more likely to make a move, especially if a TDI cross and/or APB colour change is in play.  It will also help to reduce your screen time and the number of trades and therefore stop the overtrading.

Trade durations can be anything from a day to several weeks with a disciplined approach to Stop Loss management and trading the day charts takes out a lot of noise and false signals.

The TDI TSL for me is a very strong indicator - if it is on a trend run from 32 to 68 or 68 to 32, then it is most often telling you that the the momentum has been established and to stay in the trade.

Hope this helps - happy pip hunting

4th add-on now in play - so what this means is that when the pair stalls / pulls back, for every 1 pip pull back, that is 4 lost pips - this is where you need to stick to the trading plan and manage the SL settings and ensure that combined lost pips do not kill your profits too much. This is all down to risk tolerance for the individual trader - no real set rules here - how many pips can you stand to lose? If this trade continues and fully recovers the prior drop, there is at least another 100pips to go, which equates to an additional 400pips, or if it retraces, it loses 200pips of profit and the end result is +200.

The real test is when it is real money and not a demo account - this is my live account, so real $$$ at stake here.
