--- 帖子 #2011 ---
Pivot - Everything should be in Post #1 - the indicator is ATR Pips UL Corner

Short Summary - If ATR7=100pips, then ATR 1 for the APB colour change should be 75pips - however, I would be OK with 50% or 50pips. when the APB changes colour, there needs to be a reasonable body size - not all wicks, so I initially came up with 75% as a test. If you enter on really small candles, the move generally loses momentum. I have attached a snapshot of my data window so you can see it in action.

the APB Guidelines were posted last year and may be of use

Indicators for Chart (Day)

Synergy_APB_[C]

ATR Pips UL Corner – color to none - periods 1 – multiplier 1 - this will give you the ATR for a single candle

ATR Pips UL Corner – color to none - periods 7 – multiplier 1 (read dcginc posts for using this and setting SL and TP)

EMA 200 – blue dotted – Price Typical

EMA 7 - Price typical - shift = 1

Fractals (Bill Williams)

Supply and Demand indicator II_SupDem

--- 帖子 #2027 ---
One of the approaches is to use the ATR7 value.  The approach from dcginc was to to set the initial SL to 2XATR7, so depending on the pair and its daily range, that could be 300pips, or swing high / swing low, whichever is the lower value.  The worst DD I have seen is 150 - 175 pips.  At this time it is usually close to stopping out, so leaving it to run is no real additional risk.  The difficult aspect is when PA goes 80 pips down and sits there for 2 days!  If you lose the signal / entry criteria completely, then it can be worthwhile to kill the trade and wait for the next set-up - difficult decision.

Typically if the price moves into profit and hits the TP1 level which will be 1XATR7, and then move TP2 to BE, there is a good probability for higher profits - at least worst case is TP1 = 1XATR7 and a TP2 @ BE.

--- 帖子 #2037 ---
Usually I am moving the SL behind each day so using the previous day low or the day before that for a long.  IF PA is nearing S/R levels and I see indicators stalling / reversing, I may take a manual exit (and then complain about the additional 100pips I could have got if I stayed in )

One thing that most of the old timers wiil tell you that once an indicator is in the OverSold / OverBought region, they are unreliable, so difficult to use - base all decisions on PA at this point, so if PA starts to reverse and TDI is above 68, consider exiting and saving the pips.

Taking a 2 lot strategy helps to put some early pips in the bank, but using 1 lot for entry and then adding on after the entry ART7 value has been passed will still give very good yields and does reduce your entry risk by 50%.

There will be the occasional loss where both entries get taken out (this will usually occur in the first 3 candles as an Engulfing candle - mostly from a news event, so look ahead at the upcoming news - watch out for for red flag events - I never place trades before NFP and FOMC releases), but I only see this on less than 10% of my trades - the pips won on the bigger trends easily cover that.

--- 帖子 #2047 ---
Tia,

My rules for day trading are to base all trade decisions off of the previous day close - I review charts during the Asian Sessions, which is 5pm to 8pm Pacific.  If there is a strong move in the first 3 hours of the new candle and confirms the previous PA direction, then it can be taken as an entry.

Another strong rule is to trade in the direction of the TDI Trade Signal Line.  If the TSL is heading up, ignore any RSI Price Line crosses that are opposite to TSL.

Remember, we are looking for larger pip gains on the day charts - If a pair does not have the possibility of moving 100pips, then we should question whether it is the right pair to trade - there are plenty out there that move 100+pips.

--- 帖子 #2049 ---
Tia,

another rule to watch for is once you have a TDI Cross and a colour change on the APB, make sure you enter on the 1st or 2nd candle.  The 3rd candle after the TDI cross is too late.

--- 帖子 #2089 ---
From Post #1:

SL and TP levels:

From the TMS thread - dcginc posted several posts on setting up SL and TP levels using the ATR(7) and I have tweaked this to match my approach.

I now run with 3 entries per set-up and base my SL on the current ATR(7) - usually 1.5XATR(7) or the previous swing H/L / Fractal - this will mean SL levels are sometimes 200 + pips on the more volatile pairs.

TP1 for reversals is 1.5XATR(7)

TP2 - options here are to set TP2 at 3XATR(7), OR, for TP2, you can always leave this open and manually manage the trade. My suggestion is to start out wit the fixed

TP3 - no fixed level - run with manually adjusting SL levels

Experiment with TP1 and TP2, see how it works, modify as necessary, but don't allow the greed glands to take over your trading plan

Once TP1 is hit, move TP2 and TP3 to B/E and then manage to your trading plan.

--- 帖子 #2099 ---
with regards to the 233ema, this was a style that Big E was testing with a 23 ema.

I have since reverted to the 200ema and dropped the 23ema.

If price is moving towards the 200ema, you need to have at least the ATR7 value of pips space between PA and the 200ema to make it worthwhile, as PA will often pause / bounce back off the 200ema.

If PA breaks through the 200ema, then consider setting your SL at least 50 pips on the other side of it to give the PA some room to move.  See my comments in post # 2102

--- 帖子 #2102 ---
Weekly charts take a while to reverse and generate a TDI cross, the weekly will typically lag the day chart by a few days.

For reversals, you could wait for the APB/HA bar to change colour before verifying on the Day chart, but you will miss out on the earlier day chart entries.

I prefer to operate mainly on the day charts and use these to judge the trend - you can still take the weekly charts for setting the S/R levels and these often provide a good signal for reversals.  If you have a strong weekly trend, then a day reversal is often a minor pullback/pause before resumption of the trend.

Additionally with the day TDI, entries with the RSI Price line and TSL both heading in the same direction as PA are the stronger entries, especially when they are coming out of the 32 / 68 zones, or the RSI is bouncing off of the TSL, as this gives a better confirmation of the move.  Price bounces off of the 200EMA together with a TDI cross are also strong entries.  IF the TSL is flat, this is often a sign of price consolidation.

--- 帖子 #2109 ---
Helanka,

I was creating this post last week so your question is well timed and addresses an issue that many traders struggle with.

Risk / Money Management

When looking at % of account risk per trade, your initial % at risk can only be calculated once you know your Trade Size, your Stop Loss and your trading account leverage.

For Example:

Account Balance = $1,000

Trade Size / Lots = 0.05 = $50

Account Leverage = 100:1

Stop Loss = 100pips

With the above settings, your Total $ at risk = $50, which means that your % of Account at Risk = 5%

If your Stop Loss is set to 200pips, then your Total $ at risk = $100, which means that the you’re your Account at Risk = 10%.  If you are trading with multiple entries, then this amount would be at risk for each trade entered.

The example for using the ATR(7) at trade entry for setting Stop Loss would look like this:

ATR(7) = 120pips

Stop Loss = 1.5XATR(7) = 180pips

Account Balance = $1,000

Trade Size / Lots = 0.05 = $50

Account Leverage = 100:1

With the above settings, your Total $ at risk = $90, which means that your % of Account at Risk = 9%.  If the Account % being risked is too high, reduce the trade size.  If you reduce the Stop Loss, all you do is pretty much guarantee that the trade will get stopped out.

The attached spreadsheet may help

Welcome - From what I see on your chart you have the ATR loaded - it's in the top left of your screen. Use your Data Window to see the values.

From post#1

Indicators for Chart (Day)

Synergy_APB_[C]

ATR Pips UL Corner – color to none - periods 1 – multiplier 1 - this will give you the ATR for a single candle

ATR Pips UL Corner – color to none - periods 7 – multiplier 1 (read dcginc posts for using this and setting SL and TP)

EMA 200 – blue dotted – Price Typical

EMA 100 – aqua dotted – Price Typical

Fractals (Bill Williams)

Supply and Demand indicator II_SupDem - optional

Indicator Window 1

TMSTDI Watchdog – all settings at defaults – Set the alarms that you do not want to false and adjust the font sizes accordingly for your set-up. Colors are personal preference for the TDI lines - I do not use the "Bollinger" lines, so I stick with TSL / RSI and MBL

Overlay the RSI set to 10 with no color – just a personal preference – higher probability trades when RSI(10) is above 51 for longs and below 49 for shorts. Again – another one for the Data Window.

Fully read Post #1 and follow the links to referenced posts - also read the last two or thee pages - it takes time but will be worth the time spent.

--- 帖子 #2128 ---
ZeeDeveel, I am probably just a matter of weeks ahead of you on the TMS methodology, but I will provide my comments and am open to correction.

I believe BigE would say the bar needs to close before the color change is known. Variants on this are waiting until the bar has almost closed (so close that it would be near-impossible for the price to move enough to change the bar color) or the price action (PA) moves so aggressively that the color is not likely to change.

There are two ways fractals are mentioned. The first references HH/LL and usually associated with trailing stops. The second is about support resistance and is usually based on Bill Williams Fractals (SupDemII perhaps being an example).

I believe BigE would get out (again, on close). Others will use a TDI cross only for the entry, and something else to determine exit.

You must asses the balance between the strength of entry vs. the obstacles the movement may encounter. There is always another opportunity.

You may want to pick up the TMS thread reading from October. Many questions are asked/answered in that span.

--- 帖子 #2130 ---
I may take a trade on a candle where the color has not set. This is in the area of preferences and judgments.

This is another area where you have to weigh your choices (strong confirmation vs. missed opportunity). You have both the pieces right here: You took the demo trade based on initial candle color, then it changed and went against you. If you wait for confirmation by color on close, you will have missed some pips.

I view TDI cross (or imminent cross) as the foundational trigger. Then the bar color and close outside of PAC as (main) confirmations. Note that PAC is not part of the core methodology in this D thread...I am trying to adapt.

I think it is accurate to say that the TMS expert view is that price action comes first, then TDI. But then you have the discussion about what is good PA which is where some go to candle stick (PA) methods, some to other analysis.

Generally, the TMS method is to know the price direction on the next higher timeframe. So if the Weekly TDI Price Line is pointing up, it limits Daily entries to long trades. To fine tune, many look at the next lower TF for a more-precise entry.

It is easy to over-complicate things, so I try to remember that this is Trading Made Simple, not Trading Made Complex.

--- 帖子 #2131 ---
One more thing, if the entry decision is correct and the market behaves "normally", we expect 3-8 more candles of favorable direction. So if you are using a D chart, 3-8 days of desirable price movement after the close of the decision candle.

--- 帖子 #2132 ---
So with 3-8 days of movement in our favour, I suppose precise entry points are not so important.

--- 帖子 #2133 ---
I have seen people trade with random entry points, but their trade management skills make the overall return favorable. However, I don't know that I am comfortable saying precise entry points are not important. Rather, the more precise your entry method is, the better you can evaluate your results and improve. Same for trade exits.

The way I manage my trades, I may have my stop at BE by the third candle after entry.

The expert traders know that there will be some portion of losses with the best system. So if you enter a trade and take a loss, the evaluation becomes "did I follow my system rules which produce 70% wins over time? If so, (1) nothing was 'wrong' with the trade or (2) there is a possible improvement to my method to increase the winning ratio."

A 70% winning system will have a long string of losses at some point, so you must keep a long-term view.

--- 帖子 #2134 ---
Just remember that when you are calculating / determining a winning strategy, a 70% win rate may look great, however, it is the the win/loss ratio that is the most important metric.

--- 帖子 #2138 ---
I've just been doing some rudimentary stats on runs of 7 or more consecutive same coloured bars on 4h timeframe, selected somewhat at random.

These stats wouldn't hold up to too much scrutiny but I would say show some of the signs to look out for:

Long:

65% of long trades had a small sized candle of the opposite colour preceding it

47% of the time the first candle of the run was also relatively small (so size of candle seems somewhat irrelevant)

71% of the time the preceding candle had a longer lower shadow than it's body

61% the RSI and TSL crossed each other at a sharp angle

79% the TSL was either parallel or facing upwards

61% the RSI/TSL cross was below the MBL

80% of the time the RSI was less than 55%

Short:

46% of short trades of 7 bars or more were immediately preceded by a fractal (compared with 25% long - this is probably not statistically significant)

68% of times the preceding candle was of a small size

50% of the time the first candle of the run was small size (again implying that candle size in either the 1st preceding candle or the 1st candle of the run is of no great importance)

93% of the time the candle preceding the 7 run short had a upper shadow than it's body

89% of the time the RSI exceeded 45%

68% of the time the RSI / TSL crossed at a sharp angle

86% of the time the cross occurred above the MBL

39% of the time the RSI and TSL were heading in the same direction (21% less than long)

So there ya have it! Not terribly scientific and wouldn't hold up in a court of law but fairly interesting (to me at least) nonetheless.

Most interestingly was that 71% and 93% respectively, the preceding candle of the run had a very telling shadow.

86% of big shorts occurred from above the MBL where as 61% of the longs were from below. The longs were also the ones with the 71% revealing shadow on the preceding candle compared to 93% so this implies that the shorts are easier to spot by looking for a crossover above the MBL and a long wick on the preceding candle.

And it seems that either a sharp crossover or the TSL direction to back up the RSI are important for a good trade.

Candle size seemed fairly insignificant

Finally that a low RSI was required for a good long and a high RSI for a good short!

Whether this is a self fulfilling prophecy or not?  It is interesting on this pair to zoom out and see where PA rolls over and the alignment is there for the past 9 months or so.

With regards to my day settings for TDI - RSI is set to 3, TSL is set to 8.

I tend not to bother with the RSI 10 values so have removed it.

My golden rule for watching pairs on the day charts - If the HA / APB changes colour (depending on which you use, I am using HA but I am not convinced there is much difference in how this affects my trading!), then it is worth looking at as the "trigger candle" for a possible entry.

If the RSI has crossed the TSL at day close AND the TSL is moving in the same direction as the PA (proposed trade), then this is a higher probability entry.  If you want to verify of the TSL is increasing or decreasing in value, then enable the TDI Visualization to "show in the data window"

TDI cross with TSL heading down.  3 entries taken - first entry closed at +128 and SL moved (too aggressive) and was hit by the pull back for +5 pips.  Hindsight - could have left this alone for another day before closing and moving SL.

Entry 2 - continuation of trend - no TDI cross - PA break of 100ema and weekly S/R level:

PA approaching 180.00 and has broken 100ema with 300pips clearance to 200ema, so this becomes my trigger candle.  TSL and RSI still heading lower - entries set from 180.10 to 179.90 (probably should have set all entries below 180.00!).  First position closed before Friday close and SL moved just above Friday open - if PA pulls back then worst case is BE on all 3 entries. --- 帖子 #2158 ---
To get a feel for how this works with waiting for the TSL to move in the same direction as the proposed trade, expand your indicator window 1 to full screen and add a vertical line for TDI crosses where both RSI and TSL have crossed and are moving in the same direction.  Then pull the window back down and see what this would have yielded with regards to the # of pips won / lost.

Next step is run through some manual back tests and use the F12 button and advance one candle at a time - when you see a cross that is valid, mark with the vertical line.  Rinse, repeat and see how this approach works.

--- 帖子 #2159 ---
Just saw the following re-posted on the TMS thread which was a post from Big E as he was teaching on what he looks for before each entry - worth re-posting here

Your safest trades will always be when green crosses red and you enter on candle 1 or 2... odds are in your favor. Why? Because I'm expecting 3-8 candles... which is average...

With bounce trades the odds are lower for your success... but it still works.

When wanting to enter a TDI trade... take a moment first to observe basic 4x things... like:

How close am I to the previous high or lo (for the day charts this will be the weekly S/R levels)

Am I in an uptrend or downtrend.. short & long term... (for the day charts, we are usually looking for reversals or trend continuations after a pause)

Am I in or close to a consolidation area

Are the previous candles small...

Look at the candles on the last reversal... big, little, what

How does the momentum look right now (12-2, 4-6) (referring to the TDI momentum with regards to a clock face)

Does Stoch's confirm the TDI signal - I am not using stochastics, (this was part of Big E's original method, but he stopped using it.)

Sounds like a lot of stuff but it's basic stuff and only takes a moment to observe it...

If you don't already know these things... don't trade live yet... www.babypips.com is a good place to learn about the basics of trading 4X.

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...40#post4581540

--- 帖子 #2161 ---
Hey BP,

Thanks for all your charts and information.  I was wondering if you could explain how you determine your TP1/2/3?  I currently use a combination of SL at 1x7ATR or close by previous high/low, and a TP1@150 pips and TP2@ 3x7ATR, I move SL to BE on +40pips.  I have previously used different TP levels (Fibs, high lows, TDI going flat, weak candle close)

I often get a good run of 150-250+ (TP1 Hit) then get another good run up to 200-350 but then I often get stopped out by the 1x7ATR trailing SL (missing out on 80-170 pips) before the continuation of the trend even further.  Using my previous TP methods I was finding the same thing happening... closing out too early before the continuation of the trend.

So I was wondering if you have a basic TP stratigy that you use and then if you would possibly explain what else you look for to prevent this occurring over and over again.  I know any green pips are great but I'm looking to gain 70-80% of the move rather than 30-40%.  Thanks BP. Ill post a Shot of a trade on the EU I'm currently in which I can see going that way. --- 帖子 #2165 ---
If you can crack this problem, you get the keys to the kingdom

I typically place my SL at the bottom of the previous candle for long trades after TP1 is hit (1xATR7), so the main issue here is when the price spikes beyond the ATR 7 value.

Mostly it will depend on your risk tolerance as to how many pips you are willing to sacrifice in the hope of getting the large trend runs, so you can always test out the theory of using a trailing stop of 1.5 x atr 7 on the day candle, but that can be 300+ pips sacrificed on TP2 and TP3.

In the attached chart, pa gets to a profit of 480 pips, but with the SL at the bottom of the APB candle, this gives up 260pips on each of TP2 and TP3, so the combined profit for each of the entries would have been 410 pips out of a possible 1,000 pips.

Not sure there is a scientific response to your question - I too suffer from this on the longer term trends.  In the end I take the hits and look for re-entries from a new cross or TDI bounce.

--- 帖子 #2166 ---
Just my 2 cents here but here's how I do it. 03 trades opened at same price with pending orders( buy/sell stop). First profit taken when price is equal to the size of the trigger candle(set and forget), second profit taken when present tdi hooks or crosses( individual preference), let the third trade run till the htf tdi changes direction. On the daily tf the third trade sometimes goes on for more than a month with huge pips. I am not in the position,but someone trading full lots would need a pick-up, wheelbarrow wouldn't suffice.

As a little side note to anyone starting out, moving on to the day charts was eye opening for me, work through this form, understand it through a demo account for minimum 3 months profitable trading, stick to the method, patience is key to success.

Here's the current template for the TDI settings for RSI = 3 and TSL = 8 for use on day charts as well as the custom indicators (these need to be installed before adding the template). This is with the Synergy APB - if you prefer Heikin Ashi, just delete the APB and add the HA instead.

Main Chart

Bill Williams Fractals

Average Price Bars (APB) - these can be edited

100ema moving average

200ema moving average

7 linear weighted - shift = 1, weighted close HLCC/4

ATR pips ul corner

Indicator window 1

I am also a german guy, so I also wait till it's 5 min before 11PM, I then look at the Charts if there is an valid signal an then at 11PM and 2 min I will take the trade or not.

Hi Catalin,

some times the price will go any further south wenn you are at 32 at the TDI but be careful. I'm trying to not trade in these areas.

What you can make is to avaible the volatility-bands on the TDI. I think the best trades will come when price were outside the bands and come back. Also when Short-Setup comes near/over the 68 and Long near/under the 32.

When you look on your example on EURJPY you will see that TDI works flat/range on the last 10 candles roundabout, avoid this and look for a better Setup.

In october this year I've found only 3-4 Setups, on Daily we have to be patient and have to wait for the best Setups(also on other TFs). Thats also a problem for me as you can see in the EURGBP above.

--- 帖子 #2243 ---
Guys the problem we have here is wanting ti capture the entire spike that results out of the news release. I trade news quite differently with a fairly high level of success. For me it is not how many pips you make but how much dollars you make. Let me share with you three trades I took this month Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

These are M5 charts. I base my trades on M5 charts after the release. I aim for 40% of the candle body excluding the tail/ wick. That is if the candle body is 60 pips my take profit is 60 x 0.4 = 24 pips + spread. And I do not trade every news release.

Out of the three trades, the AUD one did not get to mt tp but I exited with more than half my intended target.

With experience the strike rate could be around 75%

--- 帖子 #2244 ---
And there is another strategy that I use for the wipsaw news releases with an equally high strike rate. I will share it with you with diagrams if you so wish

GBPJPY D1

Crossing up following the USDJPY cross bouncing off 02/15 close but we're in consolidation seen by MC. We did not cross EMA10 and previous reversal looked good off 09/15 High with PA. 20MA sloping down. I think this could be a retracement/consolidation in a move lower and look to sell high.

EURNZD D1

NZDUSD D1

--- 帖子 #2269 ---
Hi, Candle!

In your first example, the DB was indeed a sign of trend change. And the PA went up, just as expected. Look at how many white APBs followed after that DB pattern! That was in the past. Now we do not know if PA will continue to make HH and HL. We did not have a close above the resistance, and we can see a DT formed. The tricky thing is that we should have a downtrend now, according to DT rules, but pay attention to the suport level, cause you do not want to sell into it. We must see a break of the support first. If it does not happen, then that means it will bounce and we can look for a long into the current resistance, but we must have enough space for a good R:R.

In the second example you are correct, according to the rules, we should see a break to the upside when dealing with a descending wedge formation. But as you know, nothing is 100% certain in forex.

Have a nice evening!

--- 帖子 #2274 ---
Hello, Candle!

Nice observation! I see someone's been reading about Emmanuel7788's WRB teachings.  The thing is that I did not looked at the chart that way. When I trade on the D1 chart, I enter as Big E entered the H4. So I enter on the open of the first or second APB, as long as it looks like a good APB, crossing above/under the 5 EMA, and with TDI Red Green confirmation. There was some space until the resistance, a little over 100 pips, and my thinking was that it has to test that level. So my entry was done based on that criteria.

Have a great day, Candle!

--- 帖子 #2290 ---
Hi kohaiNL,

im a newbie to in TMS since a few weeks. Im sure you get help with your Trading Plan. Here are enough good Threads for this Topic. But please note, a Trading Plan is a personal thing. Which Pairs i will Trade? Built of my Setup? Enteringrules? Exitrules? Positionsize adjusted to the account. I can suggest you the Book "Technical Analysis by John Murphy" for Basics.

I need my Beautysleep to. So my entry is at 6:30 am before i go to work.

Dont use pendingorders for your entry. You has to look at the chart on Candle open ore a little later. At the open of the candle the TDI moves a little, THEN make a choice like "uhhh TDI steep Breech, long candle ..."

Before 23pm you dont know how it wil look. Entry wih pending order in the TDI is like buying a car without having seen it previously. =)

Dont forget to reread TMS Thread. It takes a while^^

Best wishes to you

Candle

Hello!

Trading D1 allows you to scan through multiple pairs, indeed, because you only have to do it once a day. But just as Deichkind says, you have to be selective and chose the best pairs. Happy trading!

--- 帖子 #2299 ---
Hello, Dagaco!

Well, I am trying to not stray away from the original method. I could use a 60 ema, I could also use a 50 and a 200 ema for direction. I could also use the guppies for direction... But as I said, the original method only has the APBs, the TDi, stochastics and the 5 ema, typical, shifted +3. At the moment, I feel comfortable leaving it just the way it was designed by Big E. If it ain't broken, don't fix it.

But I see your point. In the TMS thread there are a lot of traders using the 10, the 50, the 200. In that thread I have the guppies on one of my templates, just as SnarlyJack traded. So if the 60 ema is giving you an edge, then by all means, use it. The main focus is to make pips. I remember that X-man was using it on his thread.

By the way, the TDI is RSI.  It just has a MA on it.

As for your hedging question, are you referring to Neo's thread?

--- 帖子 #2300 ---
Thanks for your efforts Catalin_eros, it is true there is a RSI , i didn´t realize ,  the question about the hedging is that what do you think about doing rotational hedging, this guy was dare123. Do you think it is posible to do it whit TMS daily?

--- 帖子 #2301 ---
I do not know what to say... It is a variation of martingale. What do you do if you think the market will still be trending this day, but after you enter, it starts ranging? You never know when the trend is over and consolidation begins. But you can test it on demo and see if it works. And I did not understand after the 4 series of 3 lots are exhausted, what happens? If you are still in a loss, do you quit for the day? Or go to 4 series of 4 lots? Martingale is mesmerizing, but it is dangerous.

I remember when I was fairly new to TMS, there was a guy who wanted to try martingale. And I remember replying to his post: http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...05#post8567005

So if you keep adding to position, eventually the market will slam you to the ground. Unless you have a limit, so you stop after that 4 series of 3 lots, for example.

So only you can answer to your question, by demoing this method.

Trade safe, Dagaco!

--- 帖子 #2347 ---
Good Morning AlanGS77,

Today at my time 06:00 GMT +1 (normal entry for me) with Heiken Ashis its a good cross.
The good signals are:

-both Tdi-lines in Daily look down

-Cross through the 68 TDI-line

-Stoch looks in Tradedirection and comes from the overbought level

-Much much support in Daily and weekly

Now the bad signals:

-Look at the long wick and the littleness of your candle (Entry candle is 2 at your chart). Long wick signals that there is buyingpressure

-There are the Magic Number 20 as Resistance (1.12000)

-and the badest signal is in the higher TF look at weekly how strong the white candles are thats the KO. Both Tdi lines look up stoch too. No sign of hooking ore bending

The chance is realy big that when you enter the trade, it goes against you and then it corrected in Tradedirection. But at this moment i wouldnt enter and wate for a better chance, like when the MN 20 is crossed.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Hope it will help you.

best wishes

--- 帖子 #2348 ---
Good Morning TMS-Trades,

Yesterday my 3 Trades in demo were in profit. Before FOMC came i thought "ok lets try to trade without consider it" Mpp! Wrong

If FOMC ore NFP came after your entry, go out. If you are good in profit and you trail you SL every day ore every few days a little forward its not a must. Because if your trade runs fine and you have no Exitsignals like both TDI-Lines start to bend at a TDI extrem, you dont know in which direction it goes. I think the best is watching while FOMC ore NFP is coming.

My Trades

AUD/JPY: -70 Pip instead of +33

GBP/USD: -100 instead of +71

AUD/USD: -145 instead of +38

Total -315 instead of +142 after 24 hours lol..

For me the extract is my entrys were good and FOMC is evil.

best wishes

Hi, ejlestrado

I want to say that.

First, I am a newbie too and trade not very well. so what i said is just for a reference.

we can learn from each other. but i am not a person of authority.

Second, let to talk about your chart

MY Questions is:

1- how do you judge a trend? how to judge it is a sideways or not?

2- how to entry a initial trade? use pending order or should wait the candle closed to confirm?

For your question:

I like to wait the candle closed as confirm.

If it closed above the fractal (as the upper edge of consolidation), I will entry buy. The reasons for entry buy:

(1) make a Higher-High

(2) the body of candle is large enough.

(3) break the factal or consolidation.

(4) PA is above 7MA&100MA&200MA.

Hope help to you.

regards

--- 帖子 #2510 ---
For those of you that are interested in Cave Manager, I am attaching the settings that I use.

My settings are based on three profit settings.  TP1 is for 50% at 85pips, TP2 is for 25% at 180 and TP# is for 25% and is set to 1,000 and is usually closed out by the trailing stop

this means that your trading volume must be divisible by 4

--- 帖子 #2513 ---
I was seeing too many trades not hitting my TP levels so I took time off from trading and spent a long time testing strategies.  I came to a conclusion on the higher time frames for the pairs I was testing that I was expecting too much and the greed glands were in overdrive.  The results showed that when the trades triggered, 85 pips was hit on a consistent basis so that's what I went with for TP1 for 50% of the trade.  About 50% of the trades died at that point and then 180 became TP2 for 25%.  For TP3, this is left open at 1,000 pips and managed with the trailing stops so that some of the larger moves can be hit.

Initial SL is 115pips minimum but I will reset it to a recent H/L or nearest Fractal / Support / Resestance.

My main pairs are EURAUD / GBPAAD / EERNZD / GBPNZD as these not only have good ATR7 values but when they reverse, they can often move several hundred pips.

Again, trading is all about finding a style that fits your personality - I prefer to place it and leave it as I do not have the time to sit and watch charts - hence the higher time frames.

--- 帖子 #2555 ---
When you trade against the higher time frame trend, you need to be aware that there is still heavy momentum against you.

For the current day chart, it is telling you that there is a strong support zone below the current price action, and past history is showing a tendency to go lower, and with the weekly trend, you will need a strong signal.  I would not go against the 7EMA at this time - it needs to show signs of an upward move.

Probably not the best set up at this time - the upside look limited, so I would look at other pairs.

--- 帖子 #2561 ---
Greetings,

Glad to be back

You can create a checklist for things that must be correct before choosing an Entry.  These become the rules.  Don't break the rules.  Don't force a trade just because you don't have a trade running!

Wait for candle to close (APB Candle colour change is a good starting point) and look for:

Fresh TDI cross with good angle

+

Fresh Stochastic cross with good angle

+

Not trading into Support / Resistance (includes 100EMA & 200EMA)

+

Candle Size (ATR1 is not significantly less than ATR7)

+

AO is supporting colour of entry - res for sell, blue for buy (AO crossing the zero line is also good)

--- 帖子 #2609 ---
Hi all, I like this system...I understand how to enter a trade...but how do you decide when to exit?

--- 帖子 #2610 ---
Hi, fated

about entries and exits etc, all is in post 1.

best regards

--- 帖子 #2611 ---
Exits get to be something you develop over time, so if you are a conservative trader and you are watching the trade pull back, set a target which you are comfortable with.  If your trade pulls back 20 or 30 pips, are you OK with giving up that amount?

EelFranz used to watch his trades and take profit if the TDI rolled over and gave up 30 pips or so.

All depends on your tolerance levels and how much money is at stake.

I usually move my Stop Loss to break even after 30 pips and follow the trade with a Trailing Stop of 30 pips or 50% of ATR7 if higher.
